Public Telegram 77

A telegram from Chuansha to the Shanghai Shen Bao Newspaper to be forwarded to all national organizations, charitable institutions, and philanthropists: Chuansha County's Hengsha and Gao Deng sands are isolated overseas with a low-lying terrain. Over 10,000 residents depend on agriculture for their livelihood. This month, a sudden typhoon struck at dusk, causing a surge of sea tides and flooding the flatlands to a depth of several feet. The disaster is extremely severe, with over 800 houses destroyed and over 200 people drowned. Crops have been completely submerged, and the autumn harvest is entirely hopeless. Currently, there are no less than 10,000 disaster victims without homes, crying for food. This is truly an unprecedented and enormous catastrophe. This committee, in its capacity as the voice of the people, cannot bear to stand idly by. Therefore, we issue this telegram, appealing to all sectors to have a charitable heart and provide relief to save these distressed people from fire and water, and to alleviate the great calamity by even a fraction. In this urgent telegram, we express our utmost anticipation. Respectfully, The Chuansha County District Executive Committee Directly Under the Jiangsu Provincial Branch of the Chinese Kuomintang.

Mei Yilin Visits Shandong to Inspect Disaster Areas 78

| | To Return to Beijing in One Week to Report | |

A Jining correspondence reports that today (the 7th) at 11:45 AM, Mei Yilin, a special envoy from the Central Government, arrived in Yanzhou from Beijing via the Tianjin-Pukou No. 2 train to investigate the disaster situation in Western Shandong. When Mei arrived at Yanzhou Station, Li Shuchun, Director of the Civil Affairs Department, Xin Zhujiu, Standing Committee Member of the Provincial Relief Committee, and others were at the station to greet him. After Mei disembarked, he went with Li and Xin to Jindehui to rest. According to Mei, the mission and thoughts of this trip were as follows: "I am here purely to inspect the disaster situation in Shandong Province. I have also met with the representatives of Shandong who are petitioning for relief in Beijing. Because Minister Song is attending the Lushan Conference, he is very concerned about the flood disaster, so he specially sent me to inspect the disaster area to determine the allocation of relief funds and the overall plan for disaster relief. It is reported that the disaster in Shandong this time was unexpected. Both Minister Song and I are very clear about this. Originally, the flood control measures of Shandong River Works were handled by Chairman Han and were extremely solid. I have also heard that the county magistrates in charge of river management are guarding the dikes at all times, exceeding even the defenses of the sages of the past. Unfortunately, the breach of the long dike in Hebei caused the flowing water to affect Shandong Province, resulting in this huge disaster, which is very regrettable. Chairman Yu Xuezhong of Hebei, who was recently in Beijing, spoke about this matter and was also deeply apologetic, but it was really beyond human power. Fortunately, Chairman Han tried his best to prevent and control the situation earlier and raised and petitioned for relief later, so he can be considered to have done his duty to the people and is very admirable. I urgently want to see the disaster situation first. If there is a railcar to save time, I will immediately go to Jining because Minister Song will return to Beijing in one week, so I will report first in one or two days so that I can go to Kaifeng and Lanfeng for inspection as soon as possible. I will return to Beijing in about a week." After speaking, he and Li and Xin boarded the original special train at 1:30 PM and headed to Jining. The train traveled very fast, arriving in Jining at 2:30 PM. Military police were on guard at the station. After Mei and others disembarked, they took a car to the Jifeng Flour Mill to meet with representatives of the disaster victims and inquire about the disaster situation. County Magistrate Lin Kaitai, along with Brigade Commander Zhang Shulin, visited Mei and Li and reported on the recent flood situation, saying that Chairman Han's special train had transported refugees. Because the refugees still had a good autumn harvest, it was difficult to move their homes, so they had not gone elsewhere. Mei and Li comforted the representatives with kind words. That evening, Mei telegraphed to summon the county magistrates of the disaster areas to come to Jining quickly to inquire about everything in person. At 5:00 AM tomorrow (the 8th), he took a boat from the canal into the Shushui River to survey the disaster areas at the border between Jining, Jiaxiang, Wenshang, Junlukou, and Jinxiang.

Page 14

After the district, he turned back to Jinan that night. At 4:00 AM on the 9th, he transferred to a car and went to Puyuan and Shouyang counties, planning to return to Jinan that night to meet with Han and then turn to Kaifeng and Lanfeng to inspect everything. (7th)

He and Zhang Telegraph the Central Government to Resolve the Hankou Postal Strike 79

Postal Workers' Union Has Sent Representatives to Hankou to Mediate

Municipal Party Committee and Municipal Government Convene Mediation Meeting

A correspondence from Hankou reports that the Hankou postal workers' strike, which began on the 5th and has drawn the attention of society, has reached its deadline today. Director-General Shi Missi has not yet provided a satisfactory response, and various parties are deeply concerned about this. To prevent the situation from escalating, the National Postal Workers' Union has specially dispatched Standing Committee Members Lu Jingshi and Zhao Shusen to Hankou to be responsible for mediation. They have already arrived in Beijing from Shanghai and contacted Minister of Communications Zhu Jiahua. According to Lu and Zhao, the Ministry of Communications has no prejudices against the workers' demands and can resolve the matter satisfactorily. They will also come to Hankou from Beijing. Although the Post Office has not yet received a reply telegram from the Ministry of Communications, the atmosphere has been eased somewhat. Pacification Commissioner He Chengjun and Provincial Government Chairman Zhang Qun believe that the postal service is extremely important to transportation and should not be allowed to have any more unfortunate incidents. They have telegraphed the Central Government and the Ministry of Communications separately, requesting that they quickly find a way to resolve the matter. The Hankou Special Municipality Party Committee and Municipal Government also jointly convened a mediation meeting on the 8th. The Municipal Party Committee sent Standing Committee Member Wu Shaoshu, and the Municipal Government sent Mayor Wu Guozhen. Han Dayong, Ning Kuanchen, Zhang Enze, Zeng Qingzao, Li Shujie, Dai Songqiao, Chen Liang, and Wang Dingyi, executive committee members of the Postal Workers' Union, and Wang Bangxin, Zhang Taihua, Peng Shizhen, Yin Jiechao, Luo Ziqi, Li Xianglin, and Zhang Xuxun, supervisory committee members, and workers' representatives Li Liqiang, Hu Ke, Liu Wenbing, Peng Haiqing, Guo Yizhang, Tang Yaohuang, Shi Wenan, Li Xiaochun, Zhang Shiyuan, and Liu Jichang all attended. Wu Shaoshu and Wu Guozhen repeatedly urged them to negotiate peacefully. As a result, it was decided to await the telegram from the Central Government and the Ministry of Communications to Hankou and then discuss the matter further. In addition, the Wuhan Garrison Headquarters expressed its opinion, saying that it was regrettable that the postal workers went on strike for two hours. During this period of suppressing the Red bandits, any strike is sufficient to endanger public security and is not only an economic loss. Moreover, postal personnel are one type of national civil servant, and their work has a global nature, so it cannot be regarded as a local issue. If postal workers have any objections to the government's handling of the matter, they can peacefully request a resolution through legitimate and legal means. If, unfortunately, a strike or work slowdown occurs, disrupting the order and tranquility of Wuhan, the headquarters will have to take emergency suppression measures based on its position. (8th)

He Chengjun Convenes Military Conference 80

All Generals from Eastern Hubei Attend

Decide on Plans for Bandit Suppression, Village Clearing, and Post-Disaster Relief

A correspondence from Hankou reports that He Chengjun, Pacification Commissioner stationed in Hubei, departed from Hankou on the 7th to inspect Eastern Hubei, passing through Huangpi and Qiting before arriving at Songbu. The generals from nearby areas had gathered there in advance to greet him. Because He was tired from the car journey, he only inquired about the recent situation of bandit suppression in various places and the actual situation of the people that evening. On the morning of the 8th, at 9:00 AM, he formally held a military conference. The attending generals included Sun Lianzhong, Commander-in-Chief of the 26th Route Army, Liu Maoen, Commander-in-Chief of the 1st Column, Shangguan Yunxiang, Commander-in-Chief of the 2nd Column, Hao Mengling, Commander of the 9th Army, Peng Zhenshan, Commander of the 30th Army, Wan Yaohuang, Commander of the 13th Division, Song Tiancai, Commander of the 75th Division, Gan Fang, Chief of Staff of the 2nd Column Headquarters, and Xu Liding, Chief of Staff of the 45th Division. The scope of discussion included: (1) Bandit Suppression, (2) Village Clearing, (3) Post-Disaster Relief. It is reported that new plans have been decided and will be implemented step by step. In general, within bandit-infested areas, they will use all their strength to suppress and destroy the main force; in semi-bandit-infested areas, they will implement village clearing to annihilate the remnants; in bandit-free areas, they will assist the local government in handling post-disaster relief and restoring vitality. He will stay in Songbu for two more days and then go to Huangma and other places for inspection. The generals are scheduled to return to their respective defenses on the 9th. To provide relief to the refugees in the area, the Provincial Government has twice ordered the Civil Affairs Department to allocate relief funds: 15,000 yuan were allocated the first time, with Zhong Wenzao in charge of distribution; 20,000 yuan were allocated the second time, with Lei Binghun in charge of distribution. A refugee camp was also established at Qiliping in Huang'an. The number of refugees returning from the bandit areas is increasing daily, and the benefits are considerable.

Liu Zhenhua, Commander-in-Chief of the Henan-Hubei-Anhui Border Area Bandit Suppression, believing that Chairman Chiang had issued an edict to employ local gentry, following the examples of Zeng and Hu, and that it was necessary to engage in the restoration of rural villages as the bandit areas were successively recovered, decided that local gentry were the most suitable for this task. Therefore, he decided to establish rural personnel training classes in Macheng, Huang'an, and Lishan in Eastern Hubei, Shangcheng and Jingfu in Southern Henan, and Lihuang in Western Anhui. The gentry from each county must participate in the training, with 150 people per class, graduating in two months. The expenses are tentatively set at 1,500 yuan per month, with each district administrative commissioner preparing a budget and submitting it to the department for transfer to the governments of the three provinces for appropriation. (8th)

Hubei Province Has Completed Four Thousand Li of Highways 81

Headquarters Orders Southern and Western Hubei to Continue Repairs

A correspondence from Hankou reports that Hubei Province, in the aftermath of floods and bandit troubles, has exhausted its finances, and various constructions have almost completely stopped. However, highway construction, because it is related to bandit suppression and military affairs, has been strictly supervised by the Commander-in-Chief's Headquarters and is still being carried out diligently. In total, about 4,000 li of highways have been completed and are open to traffic throughout the province, through provincial and commercial efforts. The headquarters, believing that many sections in Western and Southern Hubei are still incomplete, has raised 150,000 yuan to repair the roads in the Shihe area of Western Hubei and is urging the Provincial Government to quickly draft a plan to start construction as soon as possible. Yesterday, it also ordered the Provincial Government to raise a large sum of money specifically for the construction of highways in Chongyang, Tongshan, and Yangxin counties in Southern Hubei. The route design and engineering progress will be the responsibility of the Construction Department. A survey of the completed roads is as follows:

The Tragic Situation of Autumn Drought in Chaozhou and Meizhou 84

All Kinds of Plants Completely Withered

Significant Impact on the Shantou Market

Shantou Correspondence: In the counties of Chaozhou and Meizhou, farmland is planted twice a year. Early rice is transplanted around the Qingming Festival, and late rice is transplanted within half a month after the Beginning of Autumn. Irrigation of farmland depends entirely on rivers and streams. In the relatively flat areas of Chaozhou, artificial canals are dug to divert river water from culverts in the embankments into the canals. These canals wind around the plains in a spiral shape, providing irrigation and also serving for the transportation of agricultural products. In areas farther from the rivers, farmland relies more on ponds and wells to store water for use during droughts. In years of favorable weather, after the harvest of early and late rice, vegetables are also planted. People in Chaozhou utilize low-lying and wet areas to grow water chestnuts, lotus roots, and gorgon fruit, while higher areas are mostly used to grow leafy vegetables, and sandy embankments are mostly used to grow sugarcane and taro as side businesses. In recent years, the special tax on imported sugar has made sugar-producing households quite profitable. However, the sugarcane planting period is relatively long, planted in March this year and only harvested in December to extract juice and make sugar. This spring, there was a severe drought in the counties of Chaozhou and Meizhou, and rice-growing families only harvested 30-40% of their crops. Among them, many who could not cultivate or transplant rice switched to planting taro and miscellaneous grains, so they were not completely disappointed despite the drought. Moreover, there was a large stock of imported rice in Shantou. Merchants rushed to import large quantities of Siamese and Burmese rice due to the spring drought and the country's tumultuous times, so the drought did not significantly affect the food supply for the people. The only ones to be pitied were the farmers who worked hard but could not get enough to eat. This summer, the weather has been hot and extremely dry. Farmland throughout Chaozhou and Meizhou has been cracked by the sun, and seedlings have withered. Sugarcane and orchards have completely withered. At that time, farmers tried their best to remedy the situation. To avoid the scorching sun, they would go to the fields to irrigate in the evening, drawing water into the fields all night long. Family members, fathers, sons, men, women, old and young, took turns working until the next morning. However, it had been a long time without rain, and the rivers, canals, ponds, and marshes were completely dry. There was no water to irrigate, and no water to draw. At this point, they were at a loss, waiting for death. In the coastal counties of Chaoyang, Jieyang, Huilai, Raoping, Chenghai, because the upstream rivers had dried up, at first, each village blocked the river channels in the rivers to store water for irrigation. This not only hindered traffic but also caused water disputes and fights in the villages. However, as the river water dried up, the tides rose higher and higher, and the river water became salty. When farmers used it to irrigate their fields, the rice seedlings all rotted. In Chaoyang County, a type of pest similar to locusts emerged. Because the soil was dry, the insects crawled out of the mud and first ate the stalks of the ears. As the insects grew wings, they flew to other fields and multiplied easily. Moreover, during the drought, the northwest wind blew every morning and evening. When the wind blew, the heat felt like fanning a fire. The temperature at noon was often between 94 and 96 degrees, causing farmers in various counties to suffer from heatstroke and vomiting while working hard in the heat. Many children died from dysentery, and livestock such as cattle, pigs, and chickens suffered from epidemics. In Fengshun, almost no chicks were left to breed. According to the Chaozhou and Meizhou seasonal calendar, the southeast wind should blow after the Beginning of Autumn. When the east wind rises, yellow croaker from the sea come to market. When the south wind rises, there is rain and dew, and the fields can be moistened. However, the weather this autumn is abnormal. The northwest wind blows every morning and the southwest wind blows every afternoon. People feel thirsty, and excessive drinking or seeking coolness leads to illness. The fields have been exposed to the sun and scorched by the wind. The heat has dried everything up. Heaven's will is such that it cannot be remedied by human effort. The spring drought has just passed, and the autumn drought has come again. The tax burden on the people is increasing day by day. What can we do? The tragic situation has already occurred. Fertilizer merchants and soybean cake merchants in Shantou have no one inquiring about their goods in the warehouses because the opportunity to fertilize farmland has passed. They are willing to reduce the price by one-third. (Originally, soybean cake was 7 yuan per 100 catties, but now it has dropped to 5 yuan and still no one is asking about it.) Soybean cake fertilizer merchants have always extended credit to rural areas. This spring, they have received less than 30% of the accounts receivable. There is no business this autumn, which has led to a tight credit situation. Many of those who operate this business in Shantou also do banking, remittance, and ship rental businesses. Now this industry has been affected by the drought and has had a significant impact on the market. The Shantou market this autumn is unusually cold. Although the prices of goods in various industries have fallen, no one is asking about them. Everywhere, difficulties are exposed, and purchasing power is weak. All cash has been absorbed by taxes and special assessments. In the face of the disaster, the market is an empty shell. We are all in the same boat, which is a serious problem at present. (September 3rd)

Songjiang

Recruiting and Transporting Soldiers to the Province 85

The county government received a secret order from the provincial government, forwarding instructions from Chairman Chiang to recruit and transport soldiers for application. The county government informed the Public Security Bureau and the district offices to comply accordingly. The first and twelfth districts of this county each recruited eight soldiers, and the remaining districts each recruited six soldiers, within a specified period. It is now known that the county has recruited seventy soldiers, which meets the quota. The county will prepare a document and dispatch Police Team and Water Patrol Team Leader Shen Bangda with police officers to escort them to the province tomorrow (10th) by car.

Financial Department's Tax Collection Commissioner Arrives in Songjiang 86

The Finance Department stated that the taxes owed by various counties over the years have exceeded tens of millions. At a time when the provincial treasury is empty, it issued a notice to various counties to collect and remit taxes within a specified period. If households that owe large amounts refuse to comply, they will be arrested and forced to pay. Commissioner Shen Zhenglin was appointed to come to Songjiang to oversee the collection and issue a public notice with County Magistrate Jin to make it known.

Reaction to the Reward System for Cleaning Up Tax Arrears in Jiading 87

The Finance Department appointed Jiang Shuiyi as the Commissioner for Cleaning Up Old Taxes in Jiading and Baoshan counties. He arrived in Jiading the day before yesterday to clean up old taxes from the 16th to the 20th year of the Republic, and will receive a 10% bonus from the collected tax arrears, with 30% going to the County Magistrate, 25% to the Commissioner, and 45% to the staff involved. Upon hearing this news, various agencies believed that the bonus system would harm the revenue of various agencies in the county. On the afternoon of the 7th, they gathered at the County Party Headquarters to discuss how to deal with it. Fourteen representatives from the Property Management Office, Public Security Bureau, Education Bureau, and district offices attended. Zhou Gongli, the Executive Committee member of the County Party, chaired the meeting. The results of the discussion were: (1) The regular tax and surtax in this county have always been separated. Fees and late payment fines are only added to the regular tax, so the 10% bonus can only be drawn from the provincial tax items. (2) The military advances and farmers' bank advances that the province should return to this county were used to offset the land tax collected from the 16th to 19th years, according to the instructions of the provincial government last year. This item of people's debt is nominally provincial money, but it has actually been transferred to local funds, adding an extra burden. The local expenditure is reduced by one unit, and a bonus is to be extracted from it, so the Finance Department should find another way. (3) The old arrears of the 20th year have been included in this year's budget for repaying the advances of various agencies. After the bonus is extracted, it will be impossible to make up for it. (4) Based on the above reasons, the County Party Headquarters should submit a request to the Provincial Party Headquarters to forward it to the Provincial Government, instructing the Finance Department to be flexible in collecting old arrears and extracting bonuses in this county, and to consider the special circumstances of this county and find another bonus. In addition, various agencies should jointly submit a request to the Provincial Department and forward it to the Finance Department through the county, asking them to consider the special circumstances of this county and find another bonus.

Kunshan

A Fight Leads to a Murder 88

Xia Yunsheng, a farmer in Tangzhuang Village, five miles from the city, had an argument with Fei Afu, a servant of Mao Guisheng's family in the same village, around 6:00 PM on the 7th. First, they cursed at each other, then they started fighting. Xia then used an iron shovel to crack Fei Afu's head, and blood flowed continuously. After being hit, Fei dared not show weakness and stabbed Xia in the abdomen several times with a small knife left behind by the army before escaping. After being stabbed, Xia died in the evening due to excessive blood loss. At 5:00 AM on the 8th, the murderer Fei Afu learned of this and surrendered to the Public Security Police Station outside Xiaoximen. Section Chief Dong immediately went to Tangzhuang to investigate and took Xia's widow, Xia Xia, to the station along with the murderer Fei Afu to be handed over to the County Bureau, which reported to the County Government to send personnel to examine the body. County Magistrate Cheng, upon receiving the report, appointed Yin Youxin, the Chief of the First Section of the Public Security Bureau, to take the examiner to the countryside to examine the body. It was found that Xia Yunsheng had been stabbed in the abdomen and died. He filled out the coroner's report and ordered the family to collect the body and return to the county to report.

Taicang

The Moxie Newspaper is Sued for Revenge Publication 89

The local Moxie Newspaper was sealed up during the tenure of former County Magistrate Zhao last year because it reported on business tax matters. The editor-in-chief, Zhu Tieying, was sentenced to one year of imprisonment and a fine of one hundred yuan. Zhu appealed and the sentence was reduced to three months. The circumstances at the time were reported in various newspapers. After Zhu was released from prison, he did not apply to have the Moxie Newspaper unsealed but resumed publication on May 2nd of this year. On July 9th, he published a news item titled "Vinegar Sea Creates Waves, Criticism of the Cosmetics Industry." On August 21st, he published a news item titled "Public Group Committee Members' Beastly Behavior." Gu Ruzhen, the principal of the Huochangmiao Elementary School, and Lu Die'e, the Education Committee member of the Second District, filed complaints with the county judiciary one after another. The county government's instructions are recorded as follows: "Administrative Appeal Approval." The submitted documents have been read. The case is that the Moxie Newspaper has not been unsealed and has not been registered according to law, but has been published without authorization. Gu Ruzhen, the principal of the Huochangmiao Elementary School in the Fourth District, has filed a complaint. We have complied with the provincial order to order the Public Security Bureau to order the cessation of publication and prohibit distribution. Please be informed of the previous situation. "Criminal Appeal Approval." The petition has been read. Please order a summons for a joint hearing and verification, etc.

Kidnapped Victims Escape in Dangqiankou 90

A kidnapping case occurred in Dangqiankou, the details of which were recorded in the previous newspaper. The three kidnapped victims, Zhu Ni, Zhang, and Ji Wang, escaped safely yesterday (7th). According to their account of the escape, the bandit ship encountered water police and anti-bandit troops outside Daan Port that day and engaged in a fierce battle. The bandits were unable to hold out and took the hostages to shore and fled. The police team tracked them down, so they were able to take the opportunity to escape and hide in the homes of nearby farmers. The farmers gave them two yuan for travel expenses and showed them the way home. They took a boat home and said that after being kidnapped, they were imprisoned in the bottom of the cabin and subjected to insults and suffering.

Wuxi

The Strike at the Qianfeng Silk Factory 91

The Qianfeng Silk Factory (formerly Wufeng) in Zhou Shanbang, north of Xinjiao, is managed by Manager Wang Hunan. There are more than a thousand female workers in the factory. The general manager is Zhou Yanru. Recently, all duties related to collecting cocoons in the countryside have been temporarily taken over by Gao Zuhe, who manages the machines. Gao took this opportunity to try to exclude Zhou so that he could succeed as general manager. He was very attentive to the manager but was violent and oppressive towards the female workers. Even for a minor mistake, they would be scolded severely or have their wages deducted. The day before yesterday afternoon, he advocated extending the working hours by half an hour and adding a reel of raw silk, which caused the female workers to feel pain and oppose it. Yesterday, when the factory released them to work, they went on strike. Later, Wang Yuchu and Huang Huilan, two officers sent by the Silk Factory Trade Union, came forward to mediate. Wang Axiu and two other representatives of the female workers made three demands: (1) Cancel the additional spinning of silk during supper. (2) Cancel the addition of a reel of raw silk at 6:00 PM. (3) Cancel the distinction between fine and coarse and do not allow public insults. Because Manager Wang Hunan had gone to Shanghai and had not returned, the factory temporarily accepted the above three points and waited for Manager Wang to return to Wuxi to resolve them. The female workers were satisfied, and the strike was ended after three hours, and work was resumed.

Director of the Saltpeter and Sulfur Bureau Accused 92

Zhu Xufan, the Standing Chairman of the Local Explosives Industry Association, reported that Fu Huanzeng, the Director of the Wuxi Saltpeter and Sulfur Bureau, sent many inspectors every four or five days to turn over boxes and chests in the stores and arbitrarily search them, abusing their power and hindering business. He appealed for relief. He then forwarded a letter to the bureau to inform them. However, Fu, on the pretext that the format of the association's letter was not in compliance, returned the original letter. His intention to connive with inspectors in illegal searches was clear. Therefore, he specially presented a petition to the county government, requesting that they show mercy to the weak merchants and provide assistance, promptly order the director to be brought to justice, severely interrogate him, and request the Jiangsu Provincial Saltpeter and Sulfur General Bureau to dismiss the director of the bureau and investigate him. After receiving the petition, County Magistrate Yan issued an order to the director of the bureau to make a statement for verification.

Italian Vice President of Parliament Comes to Wuxi to Investigate Silk Cocoons 93

Dr. Ge Liwu, the Vice President of the Italian Chamber of Deputies, was ordered to investigate the production and sales of raw silk in various countries. After arriving in Shanghai the day before yesterday, he specially accompanied Mr. Ma Li, the silk expert of the League of Nations hired by China, Ni Zhaotai of the Central Economic Commission, Guo Limao, a technician from the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau of the Ministry of Industry, and He Shangping, the chief of silk inspection, and others to Wuxi by car yesterday, because Wuxi is a silk-producing area. After getting off the train at around 10:00 AM, they changed to a steamship and went to the Minfeng Silk Factory outside the South Gate for inspection. They also visited nearby cocoon businesses to observe the cocoon weighing process and examine the quality of autumn cocoons. They then had lunch at the factory. In the afternoon, they went to the Huaxin Silk Factory for a visit. At 5:44 PM, they took the train to Zhenjiang to visit the Improvement Association and will discuss the issue of silkworm seed control with Director Ge Jingzhong. In addition, 139 autumn cocoon businesses have been opened in the four countryside of this county, and the goods arriving are also very enthusiastic. The price of high-quality cocoons is said to be 45 yuan.

Yangzhou

Cocoon Directors from Four Counties Petition for Protection of Cocoon Businesses 94

Cheng Jingqiu, the General Director of the Cocoon Trade Association of Jiangdu, Taixing, Gaoyou, and Shishi counties, stated that at the beginning of the autumn cocoon season, cocoon businesses in Xinshou Bridge and other places in Jiangdu County will start weighing on the 10th. The amount of silver and goods exchanged will be very large. Fearing that bandits will covet them and unfortunate incidents such as interception will occur, he specially petitioned the Jiangdu County Government to order the public security bureaus and garrison police teams under its jurisdiction to cooperate in protecting the cocoon industry for the sake of prevention. County Magistrate Ma issued an order to the Public Security Bureau and the Police Team to comply accordingly.

Ban Ye Minbu, the commander of the Japanese 24th Destroyer Flotilla, and a group of six people, came to Yangzhou from Zhenjiang on the morning of the 8th to tour the sights and visited the famous scenic spots north of the city. What Insured Persons Should Know by Zhang Sixu 104

The benefits of the life insurance system are understood by the people in European and North American countries, so the huge funds accumulated and managed by each life insurance company from the premiums of the insured can become the sacred property of the people. It is not only the lifeblood of the insured, but also the lifeline of the entire country.

Today, why do life insurance companies in the United States occupy an important position in their domestic economic structure? It is because the funds of each life insurance company are used to develop various public utilities, construction projects, and other investments that benefit the people.

In recent years, China's life insurance business has made rapid progress. In the future, it will certainly become a great business, so in recent years, many life insurance companies have been organized and established one after another. But we should also have a clear understanding, because the property of life insurance companies is the precious funds of the people; life insurance premiums are not only the lifeblood of the insured, but the lifeline of the entire country.

For this reason, the insured should know which insurance company's assets are used to develop our country's economy, and then apply for insurance. There are many foreign life insurance companies in China whose head offices are located abroad and have opened branches in China to do a lot of business. The premiums they receive in our country are not used to develop our country's various public welfare undertakings but are taken to their head office locations, such as Canada, the United States, and the United Kingdom, for investment. It is difficult to get an accurate figure for the money flowing out of our country from premiums for the time being, but it is estimated to be no less than 10 million yuan per year. This is truly a kind of invisible great loss for our country. Others use the life insurance business to develop their country's economic construction, but our country suffers an invisible loss of tens of millions of yuan every year because of life insurance, which is a heartbreaking fact. Compatriots who are interested in life insurance should be vigilant and choose wisely.

From the perspective of national investment, China now has several well-managed Chinese life insurance companies that are beneficial to the insured, especially China United Life Insurance Company, which is the leader in the Chinese life insurance industry. All their management is under the management of personnel who are very well-trained in the life insurance business, which can be said to be the best life insurance agency for Chinese people. At the same time, there are also several companies such as Taisan, Sincere, Wing On, and NingShao, which are also Chinese organizations and are good life insurance agencies for Chinese people.

There are also one or two foreign companies in China that were organized and established in Shanghai and Hong Kong, with their head offices in Shanghai, such as AIA Life Insurance Company and Cigna Insurance Company. Although they are subject to the supervision of the laws of the United Kingdom and the United States, they collect premiums from Chinese people and still invest in China. In practice, these two companies bring the premiums they receive from their branches in the Philippines, British Straits Settlements, and other places to China for investment every year. Therefore, these companies are different from the companies mentioned above that take Chinese premiums and invest them abroad. Currently, when our country welcomes foreign investment, these companies are also worthy of our attention. In short, life insurance is the best way to invest, but we should use our premiums to develop China's economic construction.

Mr. Zhang Deyi's New Honor 106

丨Passed the examination for life insurance sales specialist last year

丨Now he has also obtained a diploma in life insurance sales management

Mr. Zhang Deyi has a Master's degree in Business Administration from the University of Pennsylvania in the United States, and is especially skilled in all subjects of life insurance. After returning to China, he served as a specialist accountant in China United Life Insurance Company, etc. He is currently an inspector in the management department of the company for many years. Mr. Zhang is diligent and tireless. While promoting sales, he still studies hard and seeks to deepen his knowledge. The director of the life insurance sales specialist university in the United States is Dr. Xu Benna, who came to China a few years ago and is globally respected as a scholar in the life insurance industry. Only in the previous year was President Bu Fangji of St. John's University entrusted with the examination of life insurance sales specialists. Mr. Zhang passed the examination and obtained a diploma, making him the only specialist in this field in China. This subject is more advanced, and those who do not hold a diploma in sales specialization are not allowed to take the examination. Mr. Zhang also passed the examination and received a letter from Dr. Xu Benna yesterday, stating that the diploma would be mailed soon and congratulating Mr. Zhang on this new honor as the first person in China to obtain this diploma.

Preserving Savings and Bank Savings: An Old Treatise 107

People invariably consider the issue of savings important. The method of ancient savings was to accumulate one year's worth of produce after three years of cultivation, and three years' worth after nine years. Later, with the evolution of society, savings banks were established. Those who invested in banks gained considerable interest in addition to their savings principal. This method of saving far surpassed that of ancient times. Recently, life insurance companies have sprung up like mushrooms in Europe and America. As a result, the amount of idle funds concentrated in life insurance companies is consistently greater than that in savings banks. This is simply because bank savings have a straightforward meaning, while life insurance savings, in addition to balancing principal and interest, also offer a tangible form of security. Therefore, informed individuals value bank savings but place even greater emphasis on life insurance savings. Here, we will list the advantages and disadvantages of life insurance savings compared to bank savings, and upon careful examination of their meanings, the differences will become clear.

One: Bank savings return the principal upon maturity, and life insurance savings invariably return the principal upon maturity as well. Banks return the principal with added interest, and life insurance returns the principal with added dividends. These are their similarities. However, if a depositor unfortunately dies prematurely, the life insurance company fulfills its insurance contract and compensates according to the insured amount, regardless of how much has been paid in premiums. With bank savings, there is no compensation, and the contract contains various restrictions on withdrawing savings midway. This is their difference.

Two: Life insurance savings can transform uncertain amounts into definite amounts because the life insurance policy someone purchases always has a fixed value. For example, a life insurance policy of ten thousand yuan, regardless of its term, has a value of ten thousand yuan once the first premium is paid. Life is fleeting, and life and death cannot be predicted. Holding a policy worth a certain amount of money guarantees an inheritance of that amount. The ultimate goal of saving will certainly be achieved one day. Can bank savings do this? How many people save in banks year after year, only to encounter misfortune, death, or disability midway, preventing them from completing their plans?

Three: Bank savings lack the element of forced saving. Often, due to temporary needs, accumulated funds are quickly withdrawn. Furthermore, banks do not notify term depositors in advance when their payments are due, as life insurance companies do for policyholders, and do not include grace periods for payment in their contracts. Therefore, bank depositors often forget and fail to continue their savings plans. Easily withdrawing funds and easily forgetting to pay are not the best methods of saving. However, life insurance savings have various methods to ensure that the goal of saving is consistently achieved.

Four: The general opinion is that the interest on bank savings is invariably more favorable than that of life insurance. However, the level of interest has no fixed standard. For example, if someone named A purchases a twenty-year term life insurance policy for one thousand yuan at the age of forty, paying approximately forty-seven yuan in premiums each year, and dies from illness within the first year, the compensation received, compared to the principal, is more than twenty times the benefit. If they die after paying premiums for ten years, the compensation received is still about two and a half times the benefit. If even a small amount is spent to insure against accidents, the ratio of benefits to premiums paid in the event of an accident is often thirty or forty times as much. Bank savings would never offer such favorable interest.

The above points sufficiently distinguish the advantages and disadvantages of bank savings compared to life insurance savings. In terms of credit, banks often experience runs, while life insurance companies have a fixed contract, and funds cannot be returned before maturity or compensation paid before death. There is absolutely no concern about bankruptcy due to runs, as can be seen from insurance companies in England and America.

A Brief History of 350 Years of Life Insurance 108

One: Origins

Life insurance has a history of 350 years, originating later than most major types of property insurance. In the mid-twelfth century, Greek and Roman merchants, in order to protect themselves from losses due to Mediterranean pirate robbery, organized a self-defense group to ensure mutual protection. This can be considered the first page in the history of insurance. The modern insurance system originated in England. In the sixteenth century, merchants engaged in maritime trade often gathered in a small coffee shop in London to discuss business and various events. In this place, the method of ship and cargo insurance was invented to protect against maritime dangers. This ship and cargo insurance was the beginning of human life insurance because, due to the dangers of navigation at the time, ship owners advocated providing adequate compensation and pensions to the families of sailors who lost their lives. On June 15, 1583, in the Royal Exchange of London, a man named William Gibbon signed the first life insurance policy. The policy stated that sixteen insurers were covering him for a period of one year, with an insured amount of 383 pounds. It stipulated that if Mr. Gibbon died during the coverage period, the insurers should compensate his son according to the insured amount. William Gibbon had already paid a premium of 8 pounds per 100 pounds. The premium rate of modern insurance companies is only about one pound per 100 pounds, which should be noted. The policy also included the following superstitious words: "May God grant William Gibbon health and longevity." Unfortunately, he passed away on May 29 of the following year. Calculating based on the Gregorian calendar, with 31 days per month, he died within the insurance validity period and should have been compensated. However, after his family submitted the claim, the insurers calculated the months according to the lunar calendar, with four weeks per month, instead of the Gregorian calendar, claiming that Mr. Gibbon died after the expiration of eleven lunar months and was not entitled to compensation according to the contract. Later, his family sued, and the court ruled in favor of the family. This groundbreaking first life insurance compensation was paid in full. From the signing of this historically valuable policy to this year marks 350 years, which is a very memorable event. (To be continued)

How Life Insurance Benefits China's National Economy and People's Livelihood by Yu Ci 109

Before discussing this topic, the author should first state that because the articles written are published in newspapers in installments rather than compiled into a book, readers do not have the opportunity to refer to them in sequence. Therefore, it is sometimes necessary to reiterate previous points for clarity. The previous articles have mostly focused on the economic functions of the life insurance industry and explained its direct benefits to policyholders from an economic standpoint. However, the life insurance industry cannot be equated with ordinary commerce. The life insurance industry is by no means merely a profit-seeking endeavor. Its organization is originally seen as stemming from the principle of mutual aid and cooperation among people. Its nature belongs more to the meaning of "humanitarianism" and less to the intention of profit-making. In 1757, when the first life insurance company in England applied for a license, its petition stated, "The subjects of His Majesty, whose food and clothing rely on the provision of salaries, or the benefits of business, or the gains of labor, mostly desire to unite and insure each other, so that the benefits of the insured during their lifetime can be passed on to their families after their death and avoid the danger of freezing and starvation." These few words earnestly convey the original intention of the life insurance industry.

The spirit of mutual cooperation for public benefit in life insurance still exists in life insurance companies today, which are essentially specialized custodians of investments. As the life insurance industry gradually progresses, this spirit also expands and flourishes. Thus, in addition to the original economic benefits, several social benefits are added. What this article intends to particularly discuss are the prevention and treatment of diseases and the extension of the productive period of life. Life insurance companies, through in-depth and specialized research on human life, have established that heredity, climate, habits, occupation, environment, and lifestyle have extremely important relationships to the length of human life. The results of this research have greatly reduced the mortality rate of policyholders. Life insurance companies fully publicize their research findings, so the general public also benefits from them. Mr. Frankel of New York's Equitable Life Insurance Company once founded a special department called "Welfare" with the aim of instilling health knowledge and promoting human health, achieving excellent results. Most life insurance companies have recognized the necessity of establishing this specialized department, and the expenses incurred for it are more than compensated for by the reduction in mortality rates. This is because the results of this work have extended human life expectancy, reducing the need for payouts. It is said that newborns today have an average life expectancy of 58 years, while newborns in 1800 had an average life expectancy of only 35 years. The current extension of life expectancy has exceeded the former by two-thirds.

Regarding the popularization of knowledge about human life expectancy, no country lags behind more than China. Although the physical condition of policyholders is thoroughly examined by doctors, the mortality rate remains much higher than in other countries. Therefore, Chinese life insurance companies should urgently establish a "Welfare" department to implement health education for policyholders. The need for this is particularly acute. Moreover, Chinese people now pay considerable attention to hygiene matters. If life insurance companies can promptly respond to this demand, lead and promote it, they will surely receive even greater support and love from society. Even for their own benefit, this action cannot be delayed. The prosperity or decline of the life insurance industry is closely related to the length of policyholders' lives. It is said, "Spending one yuan on 'Welfare' work can save two yuan through the reduction of mortality rates." It can be seen that life insurance companies engaging in health movements and publicity is of great benefit to themselves. It is naturally necessary to limit policyholders to those who are healthy and have been certified by doctors. However, in other countries, life insurance companies also provide doctor services when policyholders become ill, while this is lacking in China. The author, having been involved in the Chinese life insurance business for 27 years, has seen many policyholders die unnecessarily due to the lack of modern medical treatment. For example, the number of Chinese people who die from cholera is unknown. Cholera was once an extremely dangerous disease in various countries. However, since the invention of saline injections, deaths from this disease have been drastically reduced. The author still remembers that this technique was brought to China by Dr. Coss. The Shanghai Epidemic Hospital was founded by the doctor, saving countless lives. Since this technique was adopted, the percentage of deaths from cholera has decreased from 85% to 15%. The author once visited this hospital when cholera was rampant. The rooms were full of people seeking treatment, with many lying in front of the hospital and on the steps, waiting for diagnosis. The author witnessed a patient whose complexion had changed, and death was imminent. However, after one injection, they recovered and were discharged from the hospital within hours. The rescue of their life was truly a miraculous event.

Life insurance companies should strive for health work and publicity to increase the life expectancy of policyholders, which is in line with the principles of the life insurance industry. Western countries have already done this and achieved results, so it is undoubtedly necessary for China to catch up quickly. Now, let us discuss the work of the "Welfare" department of New York's Equitable Life Insurance Company since its establishment in 1911, which may serve as a reference for Chinese life insurance companies. The department began its health education efforts by publishing health publications. Its first booklet was titled "The Fight Against Lung Disease." It was followed by a continuous stream of publications, all using simple language to explain how to maintain health, such as infant care, disease prevention, personal hygiene, and public health. Now, the scope of activities has expanded to include medical examinations, health exhibitions, film leaflets, etc., and it cooperates with various public and private health organizations to promote them vigorously. As a result of 21 years of effort, the mortality rate of the company's policyholders in 1932 was 33.4% lower than in 1911. In other words, as a result of the annual reduction in deaths, nearly 70,000 fewer policyholders died in that year alone. Therefore, it has naturally been loved by society.

The relationship between the life insurance system and policyholders is so close that it should evoke goodwill towards it in Chinese society. Recalling what the author has said in previous articles, life insurance companies must strive to protect the lives of policyholders, and their efforts must succeed. This can completely eliminate the superstitious mentality of Chinese people against life insurance.

The conclusion of the author's first article on life insurance stated, "Life insurance is one of the best methods for people to cooperate to improve human well-being, making wealth accessible to the common people, allowing for fair distribution, and eliminating abject poverty. The huge capital gathered by life insurance companies is the material manifestation of various excellent human psychological qualities, such as wisdom, frugality, and sacrifice." Now, as time passes, it increasingly proves the correctness of this statement. What needs to be added is that, in addition to the economic benefits it guarantees, the life insurance industry also makes continuous contributions to popularizing health education, improving human health, and extending the productive period of life. Health is the source of happiness. Only a healthy life has value, and only a life with value needs to be maintained.

[An Unprecedented Event Held Yesterday: Naming Ceremony for Five Aircraft] [P] More Than 100,000 Citizens Enthusiastically Participated Six or Seven Aircraft Soared in the Sky Naming Ceremony Completed and Immediately Presented to the Government The Five Aircraft Flew to Hangzhou Today to Return to Their Squadron The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, Shanghai Industry, Shanghai Schools, Shanghai Boy Scouts, and Ningbo, five aircraft of the Chinese Aviation Association, held a naming ceremony at the Hongqiao Airport at 2 p.m. yesterday, and the aircraft were also presented, took off, and performed in a small formation. =Xu Peigen's Speech= 116

Next, Mr. Xu Peigen, representing the Aviation Department of the National Government, delivered a speech, roughly stating that the key to establishing a nation lies first in national defense. A nation without defense is in greater danger. If, unfortunately, a national war breaks out, it is even more necessary for the government and the people to cooperate with one heart. Otherwise, the nation will fall into peril. Although China has had countless mass organizations in the past, they have not achieved significant results. Now, the mass organizations in Shanghai have actually purchased many airplanes and donated them to the government, which is a very significant achievement. Such rare achievements are worthy of remembrance, and the organizational strength of the masses can also be seen from this. We know that whether a nation can exist in the world depends first on whether they can protect their own nation. Whether the nation contributes money or labor to purchase airplanes, this is a manifestation of protecting their own nation. Although we can also find ways to expand from the sea and land, the air force is especially important today. To have the strength to defend ourselves, we must first expand the air force, because the air force can coordinate with the navy and army in combat. The citizens of Shanghai know to pay attention to air defense exercises, which is truly a great fortune for our nation. On behalf of the government, I express my deep gratitude.

=Wang Xiaolai's Speech= 117

Next, Mr. Wang Xiaolai, Chairman of the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, delivered a speech, roughly stating that Shanghai has already held a naming ceremony for the No. 1 airplane. Now, there are five more airplanes here to hold naming ceremonies. The Air Rescue Team has a total of eighteen airplanes, and ceremonies will be held one after another. From the surface, this seems like a spectacular action, but in reality, I feel deeply ashamed. Secretary-General Yu is right. What can we Chinese compare with foreign countries? Airplanes are bought from foreign countries, and sometimes we have to rely on foreign talents. Fortunately, we have a Mr. Sun Tonggang here to bring us honor. (Saying this, Wang Xiaolai urgently pulled Sun Tonggang from the stage, and the audience applauded greatly from below.) In the past, Mr. Yuan Zicai had two lines of poetry that said, "Ink marks on the pen and blood on the knife, to use them correctly is to be a hero." We hope that the talents in China who can pilot airplanes will all be like...

(Continued on page 17, section 5)

...Mr. Sun Tonggang, and will pilot airplanes to kill many people in the future. However, one thing is most important. We hope that airplanes will never be used to participate in internal wars. We remember the Sino-Japanese War, when we used the people's hard-earned money to buy a battleship from a foreign country, called Flying.... Unexpectedly, it did not kill the enemy and show off, but was only used once to capture Kang Youwei, and another time it was blown up for a certain Mr. Zhang. The people's hard-earned money was ultimately sacrificed for nothing, which is very heartbreaking. Today there are five, tomorrow there will be ten, and in a year we will build more than a thousand, as many as the flies and mosquitoes in China. Every citizen of our country pilots one to avenge our humiliation, and then we will be truly happy! Next, the Aviation Association thanked all parties for their kindness in participating.

=Naming and Handover Ceremony= 122

After the speeches, the naming ceremony was held. The executive personnel appointed by the five organizations went to the planes named Shanghai Merchant, Shanghai Worker, Boy Scout, Ningbo, and Shanghai School. A special commendation is given to encourage and inspire. This is the order of the Chairman of the National Government, Lin Sen, and the President of the Executive Yuan, Wang Zhaoming, September of the twenty-second year of the Republic of China."

=Bottle Breaking and Ascending into the Sky= 124

After the handover ceremony, they returned to the front of the planes.

The military band played again. Ms. Wu Ruilun of Shanghai Merchant, Ms. Zheng Baoning of Shanghai School, Ms. Chen Yuru of Shanghai Boy Scout, Ms. Yu Titi of Ningbo, and Ms. Yu Xiaojun of Shanghai Worker (originally scheduled for Mrs. Lu Jingshi, who did not arrive, so Miss Yu, the daughter of Secretary-General Yu, was invited to perform), each ascended the chair, raised champagne bottles, and smashed them against the nose of the plane. Aviation Department instructors Liu Chao and others had already boarded the planes separately, rotated the wheels, and took off one after another.

=Amazing Performance= 125

After the bottle-breaking ceremony, the five planes were driven by Aviation School instructors Liu Chao, Hu Jiamei, Gao Zhihang, Wang Tianxiang, Chen Jiashang, and Chen Qixia to perform. The first to take off was the Ningbo plane, followed by each plane in order. Another Air Force plane of the same type also flew, making a total of six planes. They first circled the west side of the airfield once, then divided into teams of three, ascending into the air. At this time, the audience in the field formed a semi-circular shape, standing and looking up, with countless heads moving and applause resounding like thunder. At the same time, Sun Tonggang's Aviation Rescue plane also suddenly ascended into the sky amidst cheers to participate in the performance. The five planes performed a low-altitude V-formation for the first time, a low-altitude line formation for the second time, a 2,000-meter dive for the third time, and a 90-degree left turn for the fourth time. There were seven such continuous performances, and they circled the city once, reaching Wusong and other places. Each time there was an amazing performance, and the skills were so skilled that there was nothing left to be desired. At the most exciting moments, the audience waved their hats and cheered. Sun's performances were like a dragonfly skimming the water, or a swallow skimming the waves, or straight up to the clouds, soaring into the sky, or flying sideways, dangerously riding the wind. Finally, he did a somersault in the air like a pigeon. Every time Sun performed, he won a lot of applause from the audience out of sympathy.

Crowded with Cars (Photo by Dagong Studio) 126

After the six planes landed, Gao Zhihang drove the Shanghai plane to perform. Mr. Gao is from Liaoning, about thirty years old, and has served in the air force for a long time. His skills are very pure and not weaker than those of Colonel Doolittle of the United States. The audience cheered even more.

=High-Altitude Parachute Jump= 127

At 5:15 p.m., two companies, the Far East Aviation Company and others, each sent a pilot to join Louis Na and Mike, each driving a training plane, to ascend into the sky and perform the amazing technique of parachute jumping. After the two planes ascended into the sky, they circled the field for several weeks. Then, at 5:20 p.m., they circled to the northeast and went straight to the southwest. After ascending to more than 2,000 feet, Louis Na and Mike jumped down one after another. After about a hundred feet or so, the parachute opened in response to the wind, and the two slowly drifted down with the wind. At that time, the viewers praised endlessly. The two pilots remained in the air, driving the planes. After the parachutes landed, the two pilots threw down smaller parachutes, and the viewers initially looked at them from afar, quite doubting that there were still people jumping down.

=Team Member Injured= 128

When the naming ceremony was completed, because there were too many people on the stage, the horizontal support under the temporarily built podium broke due to excessive pressure, and the stage collapsed as a result. Fortunately, the shock was not great, and the people on the stage were still able to stand. However, when sitting down, it slightly tilted to the right, causing a slight leg injury to Nan Huitang, a member of the music team. After being bandaged by the rescue team, he acted as usual.

=Sun's Honor= 129

Aviator Sun Tonggang participated in various amazing techniques yesterday, and the audience expressed their admiration. The Chinese Boy Scout Corps regards the American Boy Scout leader as the aviator Lindbergh. Yesterday, the corps specially requested Sun to serve as the leader of the Chinese Boy Scout Corps. Sun immediately expressed his acceptance and changed into a Boy Scout uniform, taking a photo on the plane as a souvenir.

The City Government Allocated 50,000 Yuan to Repair Damaged Dike Works 132

And Ordered the Municipal Bureau of Public Works to Speed Up the Repair

Since the hurricane and tidal wave occurred in the city, the total length of the damaged dike works is about 850 zhang. The banks of the Jun Gong Road along the Pu River were almost completely destroyed. Therefore, the Municipal Bureau of Public Works reported the situation of the damaged areas in various districts to the Municipal Government and requested an allocation of 50,000 yuan for the repair of the dikes. The Municipal Government considered the dike works to be extremely important and ordered the Finance Bureau to allocate the funds as requested, and ordered the Municipal Bureau of Public Works to speed up the repairs without delay.

The Ministry of Finance Drew Lots for Eight Types of Public Bonds Yesterday Morning to Return Principal 133

Returning a Total Principal of 4.98 Million Yuan

The Payment for the 24 Treasury Bills Will Be Made on the 20th, and the Rest at the End of the Month

The Ministry of Finance drew lots for eight types of public bonds, including the Austrian Indemnity Secured 24 Treasury Bills, to return the principal. The lottery was held at the Bank Association on Hong Kong Road yesterday morning at 10 a.m. All winning bond tickets, except for the 24 Treasury Bills, for which payment will begin on September 20, are scheduled to be paid by the Central, Communications, and Bank of China in various places starting from September 30. The details are as follows:

Chairman's Report 136

After performing the rituals, Chairman Zheng Lai gave a report, roughly stating: "Today is the date for drawing lots for the Austrian Indemnity Secured 24 Treasury Bills and other eight types of bond to return the principal. I am very pleased that you have come to the venue to attend. Now, I will briefly report to you on the circumstances of the various bonds. (1) The Austrian Indemnity Secured 24 Treasury Bills were issued in 1926, with a total amount of 2.1 million yuan. The principal has already been repaid ten times, and this is the eleventh repayment. One lot will be drawn, and the principal to be repaid is 24,000 yuan. (2) The 6% Public Bond of 1918 was issued for a total amount of 45 million yuan. The principal has already been repaid fourteen times, and this is the fifteenth repayment. One lot will be drawn, and the principal to be repaid is 450,000 yuan. (3) The Public Bond of 1925 was issued for a total amount of 15 million yuan. The principal has already been repaid fourteen times, and this is the fifteenth repayment. Two lots will be drawn, and the principal to be repaid is 300,000 yuan. (4) The National Government Ministry of Finance Military Needs Public Bond was issued in 1928, with a total amount of 10 million yuan. The principal has already been repaid ten times, and this is the eleventh repayment. One lot will be drawn, and the principal to be repaid is about 100,000 yuan. (5) The National Government Ministry of Finance Short-Term Public Bond for Post-War Relief was issued in 1928, with a total amount of 40 million yuan. The principal has already been repaid thirteen times, and this is the fourteenth repayment. Two lots will be drawn, and the principal to be repaid is 800,000 yuan. (6) The Short-Term Financial Public Bond of 1928 was issued for a total amount of 30 million yuan. The principal has already been repaid nine times, and this is the tenth repayment. Ten lots will be drawn, and the principal to be repaid is 3 million yuan. (7) The Relief Public Bond of 1929 was issued for a total amount of 10 million yuan. The principal has already been repaid twelve times, and this is the thirteenth repayment. One lot will be drawn, and the principal to be repaid is 100,000 yuan. (8) The Customs Public Bond of 1930 was issued for a total amount of 20 million yuan. The principal has already been repaid ten times, and this is the eleventh repayment. One lot will be drawn, and the principal to be repaid is about 200,000 yuan. The above-mentioned winning bonds, except for the Austrian Indemnity Secured 24 Treasury Bills, which are scheduled to start payment on September 20, the remaining seven types of bond will be paid from September 30. All principal and interest due for the winning bond tickets will be paid by the Central, China, and Communications Banks in various places, along with the matured interest of each bond. Please check the lot branches and the lot branch ledger so that the lottery can be carried out.

Lot Drawing Situation 137

After the Chairman's report, supervisors Cao Songbin, Fan Jietang, Qian Yuansheng, Yan Esheng, and Hu Mengjia (representing Mao Shijian) checked the lottery members and the lottery member ledgers separately. Then, Li Tisheng, Zhu Qizhen, and Mao Shijian carried out the lot drawing. Each time a lot was drawn, the winning number was handed over to the Chairman and Supervisor for review, and a sign was displayed, and the recorders entered the lottery number into the lottery branch ledger, and the supervisors stamped it to prove it. The meeting adjourned at 11:10 a.m.

Song Ziwen Discusses the Reorganization of the National Economic Council 139

Nominating Wang, Sun, and Song as Standing Committee Members

Responsible for Handling the American Cotton and Wheat Loan

It is Incorrect that the Government Reorganization Will Have Wang as Chairman

Minister of Finance Song Ziwen, along with Kong Xiangxi and others, returned to Shanghai from Xun on the Zhongshan warship the day before yesterday afternoon. Yesterday morning at 9:30, he met with reporters from various newspapers at his residence. At around 10:00, he drove to visit Huang Fu, the Chairman of the Reorganization Committee in Beiping of the Executive Yuan, to discuss the financial problems of North China. Mr. Song plans to stay in Shanghai for a week and then enter Beijing. The details are as follows:

Use of the Cotton and Wheat Loan 140

Yesterday morning at 9:30, Mr. Song met with reporters from various newspapers at his residence. According to Mr. Song, the main issue of the Lushan Conference was the allocation of the American Cotton and Wheat Loan. It has been resolved that all of it will be used for construction projects and will not be used for military or political items. It has also been agreed that the National Economic Council will be responsible for supervision and management. At the same time, it was decided to expand the organization of the Economic Council and nominate President Wang (Jingwei), President Sun (Ke), and myself (Mr. Song) as standing committee members.

Government Reorganization is Incorrect 141

Recently, it has been rumored that the most important issue discussed at the Lushan Conference was the reorganization of the National Government, and that President Wang would be appointed Chairman of the National Government and I would be the President of the Executive Yuan. Based on the facts, all of this is unfounded. The issue of government reorganization was not only not discussed at the Lushan Conference, but there is no need to reorganize. The authorities have not made such an expression, and the ministers of each Yuan will not be changed.

Song Has No Comment on Diplomacy 142

When reporters continued to ask whether diplomatic issues had been discussed and decided at the Lushan Conference, Mr. Song replied that he had no opinions on diplomatic issues and could not comment. He also said that he was not in a position to comment on whether the issue had been discussed at the Lushan Conference and what decisions had been made. As for the issue of convening the Fifth Plenary Session, whether it will be held at that time will be discussed at the next Central Standing Committee meeting. President Wang will release a statement on this matter within the day.

Reorganizing the Finances of North China 143

Regarding financial issues, after returning to the country, I borrowed 12 million yuan from the banking community in this city because the national tax revenue was insufficient. As for the financial problems of North China, they were also discussed and it was decided to reorganize them, and to dismiss those in North China political affairs who were ineffective, so that the administrative work for the reconstruction of the war zone could achieve better results.

Staying in Shanghai for a Week Before Entering Beijing 144

I plan to stay in Shanghai for a week and then enter Beijing. During my stay in Shanghai, I will reorganize all the affairs of the Ministry of Finance during my absence abroad and study the gains of Europe and America to make up for the shortcomings of our country.

Visiting Huang Fu for a Long Talk 145

After bidding farewell to the reporters from the various newspapers, Minister Song drove to visit Huang Fu, the Chairman of the North China Political Reorganization Committee, to discuss the financial problems of North China in detail. He did not leave until 11:55 a.m. When Mr. Song visited Huang, Arino, the First Secretary of the Japanese Embassy in China, also visited Huang. However, because Song was present, he was not received.

The Repaired Shanghai North Station of the Two Railways Will Hold a Completion Ceremony Today 146

Scheduled for 3:00 to 5:00 p.m. Today

Inviting Leaders from All Walks of Life in China and Abroad to Visit

The Shanghai North Station of the Jinghu and Huhangyong Railways was destroyed and dismantled during the January 28 Incident last year. It was originally intended to be repaired and used immediately, but the process was suspended due to the Shanghai Municipal Government's proposal to relocate the station. In March of this year, the Ministry of Railways decided to abandon the relocation due to the severity of the national crisis. Instead, it decided to greatly repair the lower floor of the building and rebuild a portion of the upper floor, so that the Traffic Department could move in to work and passengers could wait for the train. After the approval of the Ministry of Railways, the project was contracted to the Zhongnan Construction Company for a total price of more than 50,000 yuan. Construction began in mid-May and lasted for more than three months. On August 31, the Ministry of Railways sent Commissioner Huang to officially inspect and accept the work. The Inquiry Office, Reception Office, and passenger waiting rooms of all classes have been completely restored, and the Traffic Department has also moved in to work. At the same time, the surroundings of the North Station have been decorated. The Administration Bureau has scheduled a flag-raising and opening ceremony for today (September 10) at 2:00 p.m. The Executive Yuan will send Chu Minyi and the Ministry of Railways will send Director Yu Yan of the Business Department to attend. From 3:00 to 9:00 p.m., journalists and leaders from all industries will be invited to visit, and tea and refreshments will be provided. Director Huang Boqiao will report on the repair process. The designated receptionists were convened by Chief Wang Zhigang yesterday morning at 10:00 to discuss and determine the division of labor, and a souvenir booklet for the repair of the North Station was printed and distributed to the guests by the receptionists on a temporary basis to provide explanations.

Social Events for Sun Tonggang

Garrison Commander's Banquet 147

At 7:00 p.m. the night before, Zhang Xiang, Chief of Staff of the Songhu Garrison Command, on behalf of Commander Dai, hosted a banquet for aviators Sun Tonggang and Wang Zuwen at the Atlantic Western Restaurant, and invited party and government officials and people from all walks of life in the city to accompany them. At around 7:00 p.m., guests arrived one after another. In addition to Mr. Sun and Mr. Wang, those who attended included Municipal Government Secretary-General Yu Hongjun, City Party Department Committee Member Tao Baichuan, Committee Member Jiang Huaisu, Committee Member Wang Yansong, Mr. Yu Qiaqing of the City General Chamber of Commerce, Mr. Wang Xiaolai, Mr. Lin Kanghou of the Banking Association, Mr. Lin Wojang of the Aviation Association, City Public Security Bureau Director Wen, and directors of various bureaus of the Municipal Government, chiefs of staff and directors of various departments of the Garrison Command, more than 40 people. During the banquet, Chief of Staff Zhang delivered a welcome speech, and Mr. Sun gave a reply. The guests and hosts did not disperse until after 9:00 p.m.

Banquet Hosted by Yu Qiaqing and Others 148

Yu Qiaqing, Du Yuesheng, Wang Xiaolai, Sun Meitang, Dai Yanfang, Jin Tingsun, Zhang Jixian, Zhu Meixian, Xie Baosheng, and Wu Yaqin, etc., had a conversation with Sun Tonggang at the airfield yesterday. They felt that Mr. Sun was not only proficient in flying skills, but also had unique and profound insights into the principles of aircraft manufacturing, and they were very impressed. Pei Chang Enters Japanese Iron Products Iron and Steel Guild's Punishment Measures Publish Apology and Vow Never to Import Again Xinsheng Agency reports that Pei Chang Ironworks on Taopeng Road in this city secretly imported Japanese iron products and was discovered by the Iron and Steel Machinery Industry Guild. Initially, they argued strongly, but then shareholder Cao Guifu pleaded with the guild for leniency and vowed never to import Japanese goods again. The night before, the guild held a special meeting to discuss the case, chaired by Hu Juewen, and decided to take into consideration that this was a first offense: (1) Pei should publish an apology to the guild in the newspaper and explain the facts of the matter; (2) the imported Japanese iron should be returned, and in the future, they should sell 20 tons of domestic iron daily, with an initial stock of 40 tons of domestic iron; (3) Pei Chang should acknowledge the advertising costs for the guild's public announcement. Cao Guifu of Pei Chang, who was present, agreed to comply fully. Silk Workers Resume Work, Then Strike Again Factories Temporarily Suspend Operations The concession area fears involvement and did not resume work yesterday either The labor union says it is powerless at this point The Yuansheng and 20 other silk factories in the Zhabei and Xinza districts suspended operations the day before yesterday because they mistakenly identified a list of ritual offerings as a wage table, and then went on strike again. The factory owners have suffered heavy losses due to the workers' repeated strikes, so the Xiangyuan and five other factories in the concession area, as well as the Chuxin and 23 other factories in the Xinza district, have all suspended operations, and have decided to continue suspending operations today. The details are as follows: Temporary Suspension of Operations After workers at Yuansheng on Yutong Road mistakenly identified a list of ritual offerings as a wage table the day before yesterday, it led to another strike, which gradually spread to 18 other factories on Chang'an Road, Guangfu Road, Meiyuan Road, and Hengfeng Road. Fortunately, the striking workers were dispersed by police officers from the four district police stations, so the Chuxin, Maofeng, and Fuxing factories were spared. Yesterday morning, the 23 silk factories in the district jointly refrained from sounding their whistles and implemented a work stoppage. Reasons for the Work Stoppage Xinsheng Agency reporters went to various factories yesterday to investigate and found that the reasons for the work stoppage were as follows: (1) sluggish silk sales; (2) drastic drop in silk prices; (3) the daily operation is, in fact, a helpless hardship; (4) if workers can work with peace of mind, the factories will do their best to maintain operations; (5) workers resume work in the morning and then strike again in the afternoon, resulting in heavy losses; (6) if this is ignored, foreign workers will launch an attack, so it is better to suspend operations; (7) if the workers can work, they will decide to resume operations, but at this time when the workers are indecisive, they have decided to suspend operations. Concessions Also Suspend Operations As for the Xiangyuan on Gansu Road, Yuan He Tai Ji on Arabassi Road, Taixin, Jingwei, and Yuyuan and five other factories on Guochen Road in the concession area, they were originally scheduled to resume work yesterday, but in view of the fact that the factories in the Minbei Xinza district had not resumed work and feared that the Zhabei workers would involve them in a strike again, they all did not resume operations yesterday. Today is a weekly holiday, and they will also stop work. Union Statement According to Yang Shumei and Yang Gengti, executive directors of the Third and Sixth District Silk Workers' Unions, they told Xinsheng Agency reporters yesterday that the union's intention was to advise all affiliated workers to resume work this morning to avoid protracted disputes. However, the factory owners questioned in a peculiar tone, asking whether the union could guarantee that there would be no more strikes after the workers resumed work. Because the factory owners have suffered heavy losses, the union cannot bear the heavy responsibility. Now that the factories are advocating a temporary suspension of operations, the union is powerless and can only ask the authorities to find a way to deal with it.
